Results of Yesterday's West Qing Basketball League Games 98

丨Jiangwan Lost to Pirates丨

丨Labor University Defeated Huadong丨

丨The Results Were Unexpected丨

Yesterday evening, there were two games in the West Qing Basketball League. The results were (1) Jiangwan lost to Pirates, 35-36, by only one point; (2) Labor University defeated Huadong, 36-24, which was quite unexpected. A brief record is provided.

Detailed Record of the Morning Opening Ceremony 99

The venue for the assembly was arranged in the Jian De Savings Society's basketball hall. The entrance was decorated with dazzling lights, presenting a fresh atmosphere. Police officers were stationed for security. The central area of the venue was designated as the main platform, guest seating, and stenographer's area. The image of the late Premier and the national flag were hung on the wall, maintaining a simple and solemn arrangement. Seats for representatives and experts were arranged at six long tables, each numbered. However, as only the opening ceremony was held yesterday, seating was not strictly followed, as it was unrelated to speaking order. The order was well-maintained. Each attendee was presented with a commemorative badge.

Attendees of the Ceremony

Besides the 126 business representatives and 12 experts attending the meeting, the following guests were present at yesterday's ceremony: Vice Minister Huang Hanliang representing the Ministry of Railways; Tang Jianzhong representing the Jiangsu Construction Department; Liang Junren representing the Beijing Municipal Government; Director of the Social Affairs Bureau Pan Gongzhan; Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Wang Xiaolai; Feng Yunshu representing the Transport Association; Min Luobing representing the Two-Route Party Headquarters, and dozens of others. From the Railway Bureau, attendees included Liu Weichi, Luo Panhui, Liu Chengchang, Zheng Baozhao, Wang Chengzhu, Wang Zhigang, and more than twenty others. The gathering was grand and prosperous for a time.

Details of the Opening Ceremony

The chairman was Liu Weichi, and the master of ceremonies was Wang Chunbo. (1) All stood at attention. (2) Paid the highest respect to the national flag and the late Premier's portrait. (3) The chairman respectfully read the will. (4) Silence. (5) The chairman delivered the opening address. (6) Vice Minister Huang Hanliang, representing the Ministry of Railways, gave instructions. (7) Pan Gongzhan, representing the Mayor of Shanghai; Liang Junren, representing the Mayor of Beijing; Wang Xiaolai, representing the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Tang Jianzhong, representing the Jiangsu Construction Department; expert Dai Linshu; Feng Yunshu, representing the Transport Association; and Min Luobing, representing the Two-Route Party Headquarters, delivered speeches in succession. (8) Ceremony concluded. (9) Photograph taken, adjournment. (10) Banquet.

Chairman's Opening Remarks

Chairman Liu Weichi said in his opening remarks: "Today marks the first day of the Two-Route Business Conference. We are honored by the presence of representatives and experts from all quarters, which demonstrates their deep concern for our railway. I am immensely grateful. I would like to take this opportunity to present my humble views as follows: (1) Report on the purpose of the meeting. Railway construction, whether regarding military, political, or economic affairs, must primarily focus on developing industry and commerce and facilitating transportation. The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railways connect the capital in the north, reaching Tianjin and Hebei, and extend to Zhejiang Province, converging in Shanghai, a major world commercial port. In accordance with the economic principles of railway construction, it is strategically located in a vital position. Since the establishment of the Ministry of Railways, it has prioritized the development of the national railway industry, especially focusing on organizing existing routes as a matter of urgency. The business of each route varies depending on its location, with some focusing on freight transport and others on passenger transport. The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railways derive 60-70% of their revenue from passenger transport and 30-40% from freight transport. However, Shanghai is a major commercial hub, and the areas along the railway lines are densely populated. Apart from minerals, various industrial and commercial activities are also highly developed. In terms of transportation, there should be significant development potential. It is essential that industry and commerce collaborate with our railway to research suitable methods, thereby enabling thorough development and achieving mutually beneficial effects. (2) The relationship between railways and industry and commerce. In recent years, with scientific progress, transportation methods have been continuously improved. In terms of transport, besides railways, there are also shipping and air transport. However, shipping is slow, and air transport cannot carry heavy loads. For long-distance transport of heavy goods with speed, land-based railways are the most stable and convenient option. Therefore, railways are universally recognized as a crucial element in the transportation sector. The areas reached by railways are inherently related to cultural development. Industrial manufactures, commercial trade goods, as well as agricultural and mineral products, all rely on them for exchange and transportation, balancing surpluses and deficits. In remote areas where railways have not yet been built, roads can be constructed first to provide support due to economic considerations. From this perspective, the relationship between railways and the industrial and commercial sectors is deep and cannot be compared to other forms of shipping or air transport. However, railways are a public utility and have a responsibility to support the development of industry and commerce. The areas through which the two railways pass face competition from waterways, making the situation quite different. Therefore, the level of freight rates and the convenience of transportation should be improved as much as possible within the feasible range to suit the environment. Representatives from all areas share this intention. (3) The past history of the two railways. The Beijing-Shanghai Railway currently has a main line and branch lines totaling over 326 kilometers in length. It began with the construction of the Songhu Railway, dating back to the second year of Emperor Guangxu's reign during the late Qing Dynasty. At that time, the court and officials did not understand global trends, so it was built and then dismantled. It was not until the twenty-second year of Guangxu's reign that the Beijing-Shanghai Railway was rebuilt. A loan agreement was signed with a British company for a construction fee of 2.9 million pounds, which was a severe constraint. In terms of personnel, important positions were mostly held by foreigners. In terms of business, materials had to be purchased from Britain, and one-fifth of the annual surplus had to be distributed to the British bank as a profit share. Foreigners also served as general managers. After the founding of the Republic of China, the loan agreement was amended once. It was not until the establishment of the Ministry of Railways that the authority over personnel matters was gradually recovered. The loan is being repaid over 25 years, starting last year. Although this year's income is not deficient, financial difficulties are exceptionally challenging due to gold prices. Fortunately, unification has been achieved, and the overall situation is secure, with unlimited potential for business development. It is hoped that future increases in income will allow the railway to be fully recovered early to protect national rights. The Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway currently has a main line and branch lines totaling over 273 kilometers in length. It was originally funded and built by local people in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. It was not until the early years of the Republic of China that the government borrowed 1.5 million pounds in British debt and nationalized it, connecting it with the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. As a result, it was also bound by the loan agreement, preventing active improvements. The business of the Shanghai-Hangzhou section relies entirely on passenger transport, especially tourists visiting West Lake. In recent years, there has been a slight profit. The Caoe section is barely maintaining the status quo and offers little hope until the entire line is completed. The debts of this route have been gradually repaid, with only 600,000 pounds remaining, and it will soon be free from foreign control. (4) Recent improvements and future development plans for the two routes. After the establishment of the Ministry of Railways, it recognized the past failures of the two routes and adhered to the late Premier's industrial development plan for railway construction. It was determined to rectify the two routes. In the most recent year, the Beijing-Shanghai Railway constructed several sidings, replaced sleepers along the route, built a new station in Xiaguan and the Baoxing Road station, expanded the Shanghai North Station, extended platforms along the route, added platform roofs, and improved sanitation and car services, spending approximately over 2.2 million yuan. Eight Pacific-type locomotives were purchased, two locomotives were transferred from the Jiaoji Railway, and two locomotives were leased. Two passenger train sets and 100 forty-ton freight cars were purchased, totaling approximately over 3 million yuan. These were purchased by the Sino-British company and paid in installments. The total expenditure was approximately over 5 million yuan, all for significant construction projects. The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway also added several sidings and purchased two new freight locomotives from the Jiaoji Railway. In addition, all equipment is being gradually improved. With the current high gold prices, all principal and interest payments for the two routes, as well as payments for materials, are made in gold pounds. Other expenses and salaries are also increasing daily. Operating income is in danger of being unable to sustain itself. Only because I, as your brother, have complied with the Ministry of Railways' intention to rectify railway administration, regardless of financial difficulties, do I not allow the slightest懈怠 in organizing railway administration to ensure future development. As for future development plans, I can report that (1) The Nanjing Jiangbian Station of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and the Pukou Station of the Jinpu Railway are separated by the river, making it extremely inconvenient to communicate and transfer goods. Therefore, it is essential to build a cross-river ferry, which is currently being handled by the Ministry and is expected to be completed in about a year. (2) The Wusong Wharf of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway is a hub for both Chinese and foreign water and land transportation. However, the waterways there are shallow and unsuitable for berthing, making it necessary to find ways to rebuild and add warehouses for loading and unloading goods. This requires approximately 5 million yuan, which is already being planned. (3) The business between Shanghai and Suzhou on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway is booming, and the traffic is congested, often causing delays due to waiting for trains. It is planned to build a change of track as the initial step towards a double track for the entire line. (4) Although the vehicles on the two routes have been adequately supplemented, there are still too few locomotives. It is planned to purchase an additional 20 locomotives to avoid merchants having no cars to transport goods. (5) After the Shanghai-Hangzhou line was built, the middle section, from Caoe to Xixing, approximately 70 kilometers, has not yet been completed, which is quite regrettable. From a business perspective, there is no urgent need for construction. But for the sake of transportation convenience, the Ministry of Railways is eager to find ways to complete it as soon as possible. Moreover, a portion of the roadbed from Caoe to Shaoxing has already been built. In the current situation, the estimated cost is no less than 6 million yuan. If some of the Russian loans can be allocated for this purpose, construction can begin. (6) The general situation of the two routes has been described above. From now on, the only hope is that our railways can cooperate with businesses to seek mutual benefits. The railway can achieve increasing business revenue, and commerce can also achieve development. This is the most alarming method. However, railways have recently been affected by gold prices, leading to significant financial difficulties. The freight rates and ticket prices currently collected by the two routes are lower than any other route. Not only is the cost not covered, but even operating expenses may not be sufficient to maintain. This is cause for concern. As your brother, I have followed the Ministry of Railways' intention to rectify railway administration. No matter how difficult the financial situation, there can be no slight懈怠 in organizing railway administration in order to achieve future development. As for any obstacles in commercial transportation, the railway is willing to find ways to eliminate them to the best of its ability. I hope that the representatives present will enlighten us."

Instructions from the Representative of the Ministry of Railways

Vice Minister Huang Hanliang of the Ministry of Railways delivered instructions, saying, "Railways are inherently a type of business enterprise, as everyone knows. However, in my opinion, the business of railways is special and different from ordinary commerce. Why is that? Because ordinary commerce can disregard other businesses besides their own. But the business of railways is not like that. It relies entirely on the industries and commerce along the route. If agriculture, industry, and commerce can thrive in all areas, then its business will naturally develop along with them. Therefore, there is a close relationship between railways and the industries and commerce in various areas. The railways fulfill their responsibility to assist the development of industries and commerce in various areas, and that is how they seek the development of their own business. The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railways run through Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, passing through densely populated areas that are rich in products. Moreover, they directly reach the capital on one side and connect to our country's largest commercial port on the other. Therefore, their position is very important. The Ministry also pays very close attention to them. In the past, due to the war, although the two railways did not suffer any direct losses, they were indirectly affected to a considerable extent. During the military period, there were indeed things that the Ministry could not do to organize the two railways. Now that the war has ended, organizing the various issues of the two routes is truly the most important thing at present. Therefore, the Ministry has ordered the authorities of the two routes to organize this conference and invited all of you present to join. Among you, some are transportation experts, some have rich experience in transportation, and some are very familiar with the situation in various areas. You will certainly have many insights on various issues of the two routes. Please do not be shy and feel free to express your opinions. What needs to be improved, what needs to be organized, what needs to be expanded, and what needs to be equipped. Please bring up these points at any time. The authorities of the two routes will certainly adopt them as much as possible and implement them wherever possible. They must enable these two routes to fulfill their inherent responsibilities, assist the development of industries and commerce, and facilitate the transportation of merchants and travelers. This is the purpose of this conference, and it is also the Ministry's hope for this consensus."

Speech by the Representative of the Chamber of Commerce

Wang Xiaolai, representing the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, said, "Although railways are a state-owned enterprise, their main business is indeed the transportation of goods, which is most closely related to merchants. Everything must be based on facilitating the transportation of goods as a prerequisite, so that the railway business can advance rapidly and reach its full potential day by day. Therefore, the interests of the railway and the interests of the merchants should be regarded as closely intertwined, and should not be viewed as two separate entities. The fact that the two routes have convened this business conference today is truly a wise policy and a sign of innovation on the part of the authorities. All merchants should do their utmost to support it in order to realize the purpose of the conference. In recent years, all the national railways, such as the Pinghan, Pingsui, and Pingpu, have been under military control from time to time. Although the current Ministry of Railways has vigorously implemented a unified policy and repeatedly demanded the return of detained vehicles, they have not yet been fully returned today. The lack of vehicles is still extremely serious, and the difficulties faced by the transportation of goods can be imagined. Because the two routes are located in areas close to the capital, the order has been well-maintained for the past two or three years. Although there has been occasional military transport, there has never been a case of car detention. Moreover, the Pinghan and Pingsui routes have established railway cargo donation bureaus along the way due to military fundraising, with multiple layers of regulations and numerous items, which is the biggest obstacle to the transportation of commercial goods. Fortunately, the two routes do not have this phenomenon. All of these are advantages of the two routes that other routes cannot match. Therefore, the authorities of the two routes want to implement policies that benefit merchants, which is more likely to achieve twice the result with half the effort compared to other routes. The purpose of today's conference convened by the authorities of the two routes is nothing more than to have merchants share their grievances and benefits with the authorities, who will humbly accept them as preparation for implementing policies that benefit merchants. Those present today include representatives from the general chambers of commerce along the route. As for this city, there are also representatives from various trade guilds. I am attending as a representative of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the Chamber of Commerce is the representative of various industries. Therefore, the opinions of the representatives of various industries are the opinions of the representatives of the Chamber of Commerce. Among the various industries present today, such as the Flour Mill Trade Association and the Transportation Trade Association, have already expressed their opinions. I will only reiterate two of the most common and important requests among the opinions that have already been raised by various industries: (1) Reduce freight rates. If railway freight rates are properly applied, they can achieve the same effect as tariffs. On the one hand, they can promote domestic products and resist imported goods. On the other hand, they can gradually change waterway transportation to land transportation, and the monopoly of foreign powers on our country's river and sea navigation can be undermined in an invisible way. However, the freight rates set by the railways recently do not seem to take this point into account. For example, the Flour Mill Trade Association has stated that the railway freight rates for wheat flour and wheat are more expensive than waterway transportation. For example, the Petroleum Trade Association has stated that the railways charge Standard Oil and Asiatic Petroleum Company 30% less for transporting oil, while Chinese-run oil companies cannot enjoy the same benefits. This is an issue that urgently needs to be reformed. Moreover, the terrain where the two routes are located is different from other routes. Jiangsu and Zhejiang have always been known as water towns, and small boats and sailboats travel everywhere. Water transport is cheap and does not cause damage. As the Transportation Trade Association stated in its proposal this time, "In the past, passenger and freight traffic in Wuxi and Changzhou was transported by railway. In recent years, large quantities of rice, wheat, grain, cotton yarn, cloth, silk cocoons, sugar, and groceries have mostly been transported by small boats or civilian boats, which is caused by the railway bureau's repeated increases in freight rates." Therefore, it is more necessary for the two routes to reduce freight rates than other routes. It is proposed that the reduction of freight rates be first approved by this conference. On the one hand, the Railway Bureau should establish a freight rate reduction investigation committee to investigate and list the waterway freight rates and car transport prices of various goods one by one. After comparing the two, the freight rates should be reduced appropriately to attract more business. In addition, the Beining Railway held a business conference in the previous year where officials and merchants met with sincerity. The resolutions were mostly implemented, and the result of reducing freight rates greatly increased freight traffic, which has been deeply affected the South Manchuria Railway, which is enough to serve as a good precedent for the two routes today. The authorities of the two routes will certainly not allow the Beining Railway to have all the credit. (2) Be responsible for transportation. The key to the prosperity of freight transport is nothing more than the following three points: first, cheap fees; second, speed; and third, safety. All three points must be taken into account, and then freight transport will flock to it. To ensure the safety of freight transport, first of all, the Railway Bureau must be responsible for guaranteeing the goods during transportation. After the goods have been handed over to the Railway Bureau for transport, they are beyond the control of the lender. If there is a shortage or other issues, the Railway Bureau is naturally responsible for compensation. Similarly, the shipping bureau is also responsible for waterway transport of goods. Car transport and shipping are the same. How can it be uniquely different for state-owned enterprises? However, Article 8 of the General Rules for Transportation stipulates that "For goods delivered for transportation that have not been specifically declared, the Railway is responsible for them, otherwise, the cargo owner shall be responsible. The railway is not responsible for any losses of goods, regardless of the reason, after they have been accepted by the railway." With this regulation, goods are often stolen or shorted, and the cargo owner has no way to sue. If the cargo owner is made specifically responsible by the railway then the cost is one-tenth over the freight charge. After a considerable amount of freight has been collected for transporting goods, according to Article 641 of the Civil Code, "The carrier should exercise the necessary care and attention to protect the interests of the owner of the transported goods. If the carrier fails to exercise the aforementioned care and attention, he shall be liable for the damage caused thereby." Responsibility is the carrier's natural obligation. It is inappropriate to charge a so-called responsible freight rate in addition to the prescribed freight rate. Because the freight rates of the two routes are already more expensive than water transport, charging an additional 10% responsible freight rate is a greater burden for merchants. If they do not bear this fee, they can only watch their goods being shortened or lost without being able to obtain compensation. This is why large quantities of goods are willing to switch to waterway transportation. For the sake of the railway's business, this is not a good plan. The letter from the Flour Mill Trade Association also deeply feels the pain of this matter. It is proposed that the authorities of the two routes delete this responsible freight rate clause in the Transportation Rules and change it to "Once the goods are handed over by the cargo owner to the railway for transport, the Railway Bureau shall be responsible for them before delivery, and shall exercise the necessary care and attention at all times. If the car guards, et cetera, and their supervisors fail to exercise the aforementioned care and attention and there are losses, the Railway Bureau shall be liable for compensation." Then the cargo owner will be protected, and bank mortgages can be safely accepted, which will be convenient for merchants and beneficial to the railway business. In addition, there are extremely detailed opinions on what should be promoted and what should be reformed in various industries, which will be presented separately, and I will not repeat them to waste the precious time of the meeting. However, there is one last word that must be declared. It is hoped that the railway bureau will not regard the proposals submitted by the various chambers of commerce and trade guilds this time as demands for merchants to increase their own interests, but as plans to assist the railway bureau in increasing its business. If we can understand each other's interests and stand on the same line, then the various proposals put forward at this meeting will naturally achieve good results. The bureau will not have convened this meeting in vain, and the representatives will be able to complete their tasks. How fortunate it would be to promote national interests and people's welfare together! I offer this as a toast to today's meeting."

Speeches by Representatives of the Two Cities

(1) Pan Gongzhan, representing Shanghai Mayor Zhang Qun, said, "Since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, the position of the two routes has become even more important. The past history of the two routes over the past two or three decades has been unable to fully develop due to the instability of the situation. Now, the two routes have invited representatives from the business community and transportation experts to jointly discuss and adopt the opinions of the business community to plan for the prosperity of the two routes, which is truly a matter of urgency. From the perspective of the Shanghai Municipal Government, we hope that this conference will have a successful outcome. It is believed that the prosperity of commercial transport on the two routes is the key to the prosperity of Shanghai. As China's gateway and the largest commercial port, foreign goods coming to China must first arrive in Shanghai and then be transported into the interior of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. If commercial transport is developed, exports will increase, and agricultural, industrial, and commercial production will also increase accordingly. Shanghai will also prosper as a result. The development of Shanghai's municipal administration and the development of commercial transport are indeed directly proportional. What we hope for at this time is: First, those in charge of commercial transport on the two routes should pay attention to the freight situation on the two routes and investigate the goods produced in various places along the route. If there are any that have not been transported by rail, they should try to absorb them, so that the inconveniences, high freight rates, lack of vehicles, and incomplete equipment that merchants felt in the past can be improved one by one, making commercial transport convenient, various industries can develop accordingly, and production can increase, expanding the market. Second, the Railway Bureau should assist in agricultural publicity in the future, such as opening agricultural special cars for mobile exhibitions, etc., the influence of which is profound. Third, the railway station problem. Although this may not be possible for this conference to resolve, the opinions of the Shanghai Municipal Government should also be contributed to the railway authorities and the business community. The establishment of the sea terminal and the current location of the North Station are both outside the boundary road, in the concession. The history of the concession has been unchanged for decades. As a result, the hub of water and land transport has a great relationship with the concession, which is most convenient for the concession. It is most incomprehensible that the businesses run by the Chinese are accommodating the concession. In order to realize the Greater Shanghai Plan, the Shanghai Municipal Government should work with the Ministry of Railways, the business community, and the municipal government to change the overall traffic policy of the city. The most important thing is to rebuild the main station and relocate it to Zhenru. One end of the track can reach Wusong directly through Jiangwan. A commercial port can be opened in Wusong, so that commercial ships coming to Shanghai do not have to open to Pukou, but can load and unload in Wusong. Inland cargo ships can also reach Wusong directly and export. This is still extremely convenient for Shanghai traffic. In addition, in order to maintain the Jing'an Market district, a branch station can be set up at the original site of the North Station, and a floating bridge across the river can be built. Branch roads can reach Pudong directly to revitalize the Pudong market and avoid providing convenience only to the concession. This requires the joint cooperation of the authorities and the business community. The prosperity of Shanghai is the key, and it is also related to the prosperity of the whole country. In short, commercial transport on the two routes is the biggest key. It is hoped that the representatives and experts will take these contributed opinions as a reference and study them together, so that this conference will have a successful outcome and commercial transport will develop day by day." (2) Liang Junren, representing Nanjing Mayor Wei Daoming, said, "This conference is to gather representatives from the commercial firms, banks, transport companies and relevant agencies of the railway line, to discuss and thoroughly improve the cargo transport method, so as to cooperate and benefit each other. It is expected that there will be very smooth results. Our municipal government expressed its sympathy. Junren is in accordance with the Mayor's will, should contribute a few words to the Nanjing Municipal Government, as a eulogy. Nanjing was once the capital of the previous dynasties, quite prosperous, and to the defeat of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom, the Qing dynasty in order to eliminate the capital of the ruins, at the expense of various destruction, and then make the scenic area into a depressed area, full of desolation, completely lost the urban beauty of the realm, Now our party and the country were built here, and all the construction is very much, and all need to be done from scratch, design and implement. Our municipal government is bound to cooperate, which can be a help to the prosperity of the capital, the Beijing-Shanghai Shanghai Hangzhou Ningbo railway and other transportation agencies only. Shanghai's status is in the first place in China's national industrial and commercial concentration area, from Shanghai to Beijing, although there is a frightening river waterway traffic, but the most convenient as Beijing Shanghai one road, all the needs of the capital construction, all rely on Shanghai's supply, and this all the supply, only the Beijing Shanghai railway for the most substantive transport is the capital of the prosperity indirectly and directly, are closely related to the Beijing Shanghai road, so the Beijing Shanghai road transport more convenient, the capital of the prosperity more easy, the capital more prosperous, the Beijing Shanghai road transport is also more, the transport more, the road bureau revenue also increases. Then for the present plan, any order must be to help the prosperity of the capital as the goal, can not be said, therefore, today for cargo transport, especially the transport of Beijing of various goods procedures, to strive for convenience, freight to strive to reduce, this small profit and more transport principle, the result, help the prosperity of the capital, and the railway itself, is actually far-reaching interests, its meaning is obvious, and no continuation of the statement. In addition, there is a small railway section in Nanjing city, which is from Xiaguan to Zhongzheng Street in the city. The distance is only more than 20 miles, but it is actually an important tool for traffic inside and outside Beijing, and in fact it is also connected to the Beijing-Shanghai road. The scope of the road should be planned and improved by Junren, actively carried out, and there is also a need to consult with the road to help each end, another opinion will be submitted for discussion. This meeting, I hope the road bureau and all those present, each with a long-term vision, sent to the Hongmo Biwei, a very good contribution, the future of the capital of the prosperity, the progress of the business, the development of the road transport, are favorable, and this for praise."

Summary of Guest Speeches

(1) Expert Dai Linshu said briefly: "I am very honored to be invited to participate. Today, we are opening this meeting. All of us in the business, industrial, banking, and industry circles can meet with the railway authorities to discuss openly, which is truly the first gospel for the people along the two routes. I cannot but sincerely celebrate the success of this meeting. Therefore, I am very willing to take this first day of the meeting to say a few words to contribute to you all, and please give me your advice. I have seen the proposals from all walks of life, which are nothing more than three: (1) improvement of station services, (2) appropriate reduction of freight rates, and (3) allocation of vehicles. These are truly the most important proposals, and they are also what the railway authorities are working hard to pay attention to. I have two hopes: (1) For the railway authorities, A. Railways are public undertakings and should bear a corresponding responsibility to the public. B. Railways are established to strengthen national defense, develop commerce and industry, and facilitate people's livelihood, and cannot be based on profits and losses. (2) For colleagues from all walks of life, A. The railway should be regarded as their own business and should not give up attention. B. Any imperfections should be suggested or even attacked as much as possible. C. Cite the development of American railways and how the people pay attention to it. D. Any suggestions or requests must be legal and reasonable, and should be promoted within the railway's environment and scope." (2) Tang Jianzhong, Second Section Chief of the Jiangsu Construction Department, said briefly: "The key to developing commercial transport lies in reducing freight rates, improving management, and saving cargo transportation time. Since the recovery of the provincial capital's concession, the market has changed greatly. The rising tide and sand beaches by the river are a great obstacle to ships berthing. The provincial government plans to move the wharf to the east or west of Beigushan. As a result, the river station cannot load and unload cargo smoothly. It is proposed to extend it to the Zhenjiang Customs. It is proposed to submit it when the Ministry of Railways convenes a railway conference for reference." (3) Feng Yunshu, representative of the Transport Association. (4) Yan Luona, representative of the Two-Route Party Headquarters, expressed many hopes for the conference.

Congratulatory Remarks from the Two-Route Party Headquarters

To all the representatives of the Two-Route Business Conference: The assembly is now convened and the four sides are well-regarded. Expanding land transport is a model and compass, patching up the loopholes to enrich the people's livelihood, and connecting Hebei, Shandong, Fujian, and Anhui is an enterprise. The sound of the cry is heroic, and the progress is made every day. With this blessing, I would like to express my congratulations. Respectfully submitted by Min Luobing, Standing Committee Member of the Executive Committee of the Special Party Headquarters of the Chinese Nationalist Party's Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways.

The Two-Route Business Conference Officially Opened Yesterday 105

First General Assembly This Morning

Liu Weizhi, Director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways, managing the affairs of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, specially convened representatives from the business community along the routes and transportation experts to hold a business conference to improve transportation methods on the two routes and promote railway administration. The opening ceremony was held at 9:00 AM yesterday morning at the Jiande Hall on Fusheng Road, Zhabei. Mr. Liu and Directors Liu Chengchang, Zheng Baozhao, and Luo Panhui all personally attended to receive guests. It was decided that the general assembly would be held this morning to begin discussing the various proposals. The grand occasion of yesterday is recorded below.

Tea Party of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce in the Afternoon 106

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce held a tea party yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM in the Chamber's standing committee room to entertain the representatives of the Two-Route Business Conference. Over a hundred people attended, including Liu Weizhi, Zheng Baozhao, Hua Zejun, Wang Yansong, Zhu Wenqi, and representatives from various chambers of commerce along the two routes. Chairman Wang Xiaolai delivered a welcome speech, followed by speeches from Liu Weizhi and Zheng Baozhao, and then representatives from various industries expressed their opinions. The event ended at 6:00 PM. The various speeches are recorded below.

Welcome Speech by the Chairman Today, representatives of the Railway Bureau, various chambers of commerce, various trade associations, and various experts have responded to the call of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou Business Conference and have come to Shanghai. Our Chamber, as the host, and because the business conference convened by the two routes involves many issues of common interest to the various businesses, our Chamber and you all should have the need to exchange opinions with each other. Therefore, we specially invited you to a tea party upon your arrival in Shanghai, both to renew acquaintances and to receive instruction. We are greatly honored by your presence. Looking back in recent years, various departments have convened various national conferences. Not long after the adjournment of these conferences, the two Railway Bureaus are now convening a business conference, all to communicate the will of the government and businesses, giving them the opportunity to voice their grievances and express their opinions. Although the scope of this Two-Route Business Conference is incomparable in size to the previous conferences of the various departments, the more extensive the scope of a matter, the more stakeholders are involved, and the more obstacles there are to implementation. Many proposals have been put forward at the various conferences, but how many of these proposals have been resolved and implemented to this day? Not only is our Chamber unable to understand this clearly, but I fear that the representatives present here are also unable to understand it clearly. This is sufficient to show that the greater the scope of involvement, the more difficult it is to implement. Unexpectedly, the scope of this Two-Route Business Conference is limited to transportation, and the area is limited to the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railway lines. However, the greatest pain that merchants have felt over the years is twofold: one is excessive taxes and levies, and the other is transportation delays. The abolition of internal customs duties and the realization of it is the first issue, which can be said to have a chance of being resolved. The Two-Route Business Conference is an opportunity to resolve the second issue. Therefore, today, when we speak broadly of revitalizing industry, the scope is vast, and it is like the ancients saying, "Where to start with the seventeen histories?" It is better to focus on the transportation issue, which is closely related to our interests, and calmly discuss a satisfactory implementation plan.

Page 14

So that the second problem also has a chance to be resolved like the abolition of internal customs duties. Then, truly accomplishing one or two things will greatly benefit the merchants. Although the scope of this conference is small, the actual harvest may be above the level of the industrial and commercial conferences. As Mencius said, "Going far must begin from the near," and Zeng Guofan said, "Simple words and humble thoughts." These two sayings are sufficient to be our guide in handling affairs today. However, in order for this conference to have practical results, our Chamber believes that there are two matters that should also be noted. (1) Each representative should concentrate their spirit on a few key proposals, have a firm attitude, and make consistent demands. The common problem of past conferences has been to treat proposals as decorations. The way they propose them is like scholars taking exams in the past, greedy for quantity and trying to show off their talents. Before the event, they cite classics and talk loudly, fearing that there will not be enough proposals. Afterwards, they do not care whether they are implemented or not. There is a saying, "He who seeks with sincerity will be answered with sincerity." Although there have been many proposals at previous conferences, many of them cannot be achieved with the current financial and material resources of the country. Even the proposers know that their implementation is not easy, and they only use them as an opportunity to exaggerate and compete. The government authorities, seeing this hidden situation, then postpone even those that can be implemented, causing those who worry about the times to sigh, "There are many conferences but few successes." With past mistakes as a warning, we should be vigilant. We believe that this time, we should not seek too many proposals, nor should we seek too high-sounding arguments. We must ensure that the proposals are all for matters that urgently need to be implemented and that they are all carefully considered and reasonable and can be achieved by the government. Then, the Railway Bureau, seeing the sincere and loyal attitude of the merchants, will be able to sincerely accept the various proposals put forward at the meeting and strive for their implementation, eliminating the previous ills of "resolving without acting" and "acting without implementing." This is what is meant by "mutual sincerity," (2) For each case decided at this conference, the chambers of commerce along the line should pay attention to whether it is implemented at any time and urge its implementation. According to the cases decided, those whose nature is slightly important should be approved by the Ministry of Railways before they can be implemented. Therefore, from the decision to the full implementation, there will naturally be a considerable amount of time. The task of each representative attending this meeting ends with the closing of the meeting. If there is no mechanism to pay attention and urge at any time, then it may not be possible to avoid the mistakes of the past, such as "once the meeting is adjourned, no one cares whether it is implemented or not." We believe that this responsibility should be borne by the chambers of commerce along the two lines. The cases decided by this conference should be listed one by one, like students having a timetable. The day when the decision is fully implemented is the day when the chamber of commerce's timetable ends. Those who know the most about which of the resolutions have been implemented and which have not been implemented are those in the transportation industry, so the responsibility for reporting should be borne by that industry. Those that can be implemented within the authority of the Railway Bureau should be urged to be implemented by the Railway Bureau at any time. Those that must be approved by the Ministry of Railways before they can be implemented should assume a considerable period of time. If they have not been implemented after this period, they should urge the Railway Bureau to submit them to the Ministry, and the chambers of commerce should each telegraph the Ministry to urge their handling. In short, we must eliminate the accumulated habit of "one meeting and done" and not pay attention to whether the proposals are implemented, so that one resolution can achieve the effect of one resolution. Because today's meeting is not a customary reception, and from the standpoint of commerce, we and the representatives present here share weal and woe, and our friendship is like a single tomb, so we have pointed out the common problems of previous meetings and spoken frankly, without any checking. Our Chamber asks itself, that it has not been able to avoid this common problem, so after reflecting on itself, it has pointed out its shortcomings to serve as a resource for mutual criticism and to plan for future improvements. We hope that you will understand and be fortunate.

Liu Weizhi's speech briefly stated that the development of industry and commerce and the railway transportation business are directly proportional. The railway is a special business and belongs to the public utility business. Of course, it cannot seek profit diligently, and must at the same time take into account the interests of industry and commerce. However, on the side of industry and commerce, it must also enable the railway business to maintain its proper position, so that both parties have interests; otherwise, if each party cares for only one side, it will inevitably lead to bias and defeat. The main purpose of this conference is that the two railway authorities are willing to seek practical connections and cooperation with the industrial and commercial sectors with an extremely fair and sincere attitude. The most important points that the representatives hope from the two railway authorities are (1) reducing freight rates, because railway freight rates are more expensive than water transport. Although the length of railway transport is faster than water transport, the Railway Bureau is still extremely willing to give serious and detailed consideration to the issue of freight rates, and decide to reduce freight rates on several or part of the goods to benefit commerce. (2) Cargo safety. On the part of the Railway Bureau, it is also willing to find appropriate guarantees within the possible scope, or formulate separate rules in accordance with the insurance method. As for merchants transporting goods, in addition to the formal freight paid in accordance with the regulations, if there are any staff members who demand money, it is extremely desirable for all industries and merchants to be able to report them at any time. The Railway Bureau will thoroughly investigate and punish them. In short, the cases decided at the business conference, no matter how difficult they are on the part of the Railway Bureau, will be implemented one by one to appease the earnest hopes of the representatives.

Zheng Baozhao's speech briefly stated that the Railway Bureau's Vehicle Department is willing to use the two words "sincerity" as the aim of this conference. The so-called sincerity is: first, those that the Railway Bureau can do will be done immediately. As for those that the Railway Bureau cannot do, please give the representatives some time so that they can be realized within a reasonable time. Second, it is hoped that the Railway Bureau and the representatives can understand each other's difficulties and cooperate forever, eliminating the previous estrangement. The Railway Bureau's authorities cannot have the same close contact with the merchants as the staff members do, and therefore what they see and hear may be concealed. It is hoped that the representatives can point them out at any time, and the Railway Bureau will never conceal them. This is what the Railway Bureau's Vehicle Department especially wants to use a sincere attitude to report to the representatives.

Mayor Zhang Talks About Municipal Administration 108

Managing the Old City to Revitalize the Chinese-Administered Areas

Constructing a New City Area to Realize the Greater Shanghai Plan

Shanghai Mayor Zhang Qun held a tea party for news reporters yesterday afternoon at the Municipal Government Club at No. 43 Weihaiwei Road, and reported on the past and future of the municipal administration. As the scope of municipal work is very wide, yesterday's talks only covered the two items of public works and public utilities, with particular emphasis on the new municipal government building in the city center. The groundbreaking ceremony was held on July 7 this year, the fifth anniversary of the establishment of the Shanghai Special Municipal Government. The construction cost of the new municipal government building is about 500,000 yuan, and it will be completed in one year. It can be said that the start of construction on that day marks the beginning of the construction of the city center and is the initial step in realizing Sun Yat-sen's Greater Shanghai Plan.

The Effect of Managing the Old City Mayor Zhang said that the Shanghai Municipal Government has been established for more than three years. The most important goal in terms of work is to complete the construction during the tutelage period and realize Sun Yat-sen's Greater Shanghai Plan. However, in the past three years, it has been mostly constrained by the times and limited by financial resources, and it is shameful that the results have not been remarkable and there has been little immediate success. The management of the old city can only maintain the status quo and seek gradual progress. As for the opening of the new city, only a plan has been drafted and construction has not yet started. Now that the tutelage period has begun, it is appropriate to gather wisdom and strength.

The Meaning of Eliminating the Likin Tax and the Understanding Our People Should Have 109

Our party, the Chinese Kuomintang, is a party that represents the interests of the people. Therefore, during the military administration period, it used revolutionary force to eliminate all warlords who exploited and oppressed the people. During the tutelage period, in addition to striving for construction projects, it also used revolutionary means to ruthlessly eliminate bad systems that exploited the interests of the people.

The Likin tax originated in the third year of the Xianfeng reign of the Qing Dynasty. At that time, due to the turmoil caused by the Taiping Rebellion and the shortage of military funds, Yi Cheng, the Jiangsu Provincial Administration Commissioner, first started collecting the Likin tax at the Fairy Maiden Temple near Yangzhou. It was originally temporary in nature, but after the rebellion was quelled, it became quite abundant in revenue and greatly benefited the national financial income. Not only was it not immediately abolished, but it was intensified, and all provinces followed suit. The tax rates also varied, and it became an unbreakable domestic tax that harmed merchants and the people.

There are now as many as 690 Likin stations across the country. Speaking of its drawbacks, they are too numerous to mention. Now, let me list the major ones as follows: (1) Exploiting Merchants: Because the Likin tax rates are inconsistent, merchants have no way to calculate the weight of their burden and the thickness of their profits, so they regard commerce as a dangerous path. The central government has no unified laws and regulations, and allows officials in various provinces to arbitrarily increase or decrease taxes, and exploit them in every possible way. In addition, they engage in fraud and embezzlement, and use various excuses to extort money. As a result, tax officials are like tigers and wolves, and small merchants are like lambs. They are subjected to multiple inspections and step-by-step exploitation. Even the slightest amount of goods is often delayed for as long as a year due to the obstruction of checkpoints, and they do not find it strange. (2) Hindering Industry: Industry is the lifeblood of a country's economy. The reason why China's industry has not prospered to this day is due to the existence of the Likin tax system. The same goods, foreign goods, only need to pay an import tax of 5% and a sub-port tax of 2.5% at the port of entry, and then they can circulate throughout the country without hindrance. Domestic goods are not the same. From the place of production to the place of sale, there are layers of Likin stations, heavy levies and exorbitant taxes. As a result, goods of the same value, foreign goods, are priced lower due to light taxes, while domestic goods are heavily taxed and the cost is increased. As a result, foreign goods sell well, and domestic goods are sluggish. The hindrance of the Likin tax to industry is simply a direct hindrance to the country's economic lifeline. (3) Increasing the burden on the people: A good national tax should adopt the principle of "direct," so that taxpayers do not pass on the increased tax burden to others. For example, if a commodity is taxed too heavily due to the Likin tax, merchants will certainly not sell it at a loss, so they raise the price. The general consumer public therefore bears an increased burden. The current high prices and difficult livelihoods can be said to be entirely due to the Likin tax. (4) A breeding ground for corruption: According to accurate statistics, there are 1.6 million people in China who rely on the Likin tax to make a living. Their skills are to flatter and curry favor, and their ability is to suck and exploit. After obtaining a lucrative Likin position, they can accumulate a huge fortune in a few years and become wealthy, while merchants, peddlers, and the general public across the country are directly and indirectly sacrificed by them, falling into a state of loss of property and increasing poverty. Wealthy merchants and powerful institutions can use government offices as a shield to openly evade taxes, and Likin officials dare not interfere. The most acutely affected are the small merchants who bear a heavy burden of hard-earned capital. The Likin tax system is truly evil.

Mr. Sun Yat-sen of our party, in view of the evils of the Likin tax, undoubtedly added the abolition of the Likin tax to the political program of the Chinese Kuomintang. The National Government also resolutely ordered its abolition from New Year's Day of the 20th year of the Republic of China.

Regardless of the opposition, saying that after the abolition of the Likin tax, 1.6 million people will have no way to make a living, but may I ask, can the livelihood of 390 million people be affected by the livelihood problem of 1.6 million rice worms? Is obstruction by petty warlords and local bullies a concern that a revolutionary government should have? As for the national finances being thrown into panic, the 2.5% surtax on customs duties can be effectively collected, and it can certainly be used to supplement the finances. Furthermore, when customs duties are completely autonomous in the future, the tax rate will increase, and the income will only increase, so there is no need to worry.

Therefore, this time, our party has made a great determination to abolish the Likin tax, and the government has made the greatest efforts to do it, without any hesitation, retreat, or compromise. We hope that the people of the whole country will give great help and promotion to the government in its efforts to eliminate the bad administration. Our slogan is to support the National Government's policy of abolishing the Likin tax. Abolishing the Likin tax is to realize the political program of our party. Abolishing the Likin tax is to promote the work of tutelage. Abolishing the Likin tax is the first step towards seeking China's economic freedom, equality, and liberation. Opposing the abolition of the Likin tax is a traitor to the revolution and a public enemy of the people. All the people of the country should unanimously assist the government in abolishing the Likin tax. Long live the Chinese Kuomintang!

Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special City Party Department of the Chinese Kuomintang 110

planning and management, striving for the implementation of the plan, so that the grand vision of construction can be finally achieved. The following is a brief report on the recent work in progress. The Shanghai Municipal Government now directly governs 17 urban areas. Except for the two districts of Huhang and Zhabei, most of them are still in the state of rural society. However, although the facilities in the two districts of Huhang and Zhabei have taken a preliminary shape, they are indeed far behind the adjacent concessions. Therefore, the transformation of the old urban area is indeed an urgent task. Since the establishment of the Public Works Bureau, its main work has been to reorganize the old urban area, accounting for the majority. The reorganization of the old urban area is nothing more than two ends: widening narrow streets and improving unsanitary areas. According to the north-south two districts, the old roads are mostly winding, narrow and extremely chaotic. Because of the obstacles to traffic, it is the cause of commercial depression. Before the reorganization, a comprehensive plan was made, and the road system was drawn by districts, so that the widening and improvement of the project can be followed. The widening of roads, or when citizens build houses, according to the road system, scattered acquisitions, or important routes, need to be widened, then the municipal government will reorganize at once, step by step, and finally change the chaotic state of the old urban area before. The road system map of Huhang and Zhabei districts was announced the earliest, and the implementation was very smooth. Recently, there is a road system plan for the west of Shanghai district, the significance of which is not only to reorganize the old roads. The west of Shanghai is entirely within the scope of the road construction forces beyond the boundary, and the area surrounded is wider than the public concession area. (According to the concession authorities, the construction of roads beyond the boundary over the years, from the 26th year of Guangxu to the 14th year of the Republic of China, is about 11 li in the north of Shanghai and about 165 li in the west of Shanghai, with a total length of 205,000 English feet.) If it is not remedied quickly, the consequences will be even more unimaginable. The municipal government, in view of this, has the construction of Zhongshan Road, the first plan to connect the traffic between the north and south cities. This time, it has taken a further step and announced the road system map of the west of Shanghai district. In the area east of Zhongshan Road and west of the concession line, it integrates the original road construction beyond the boundary and arranges the road network into a system, so that it can be connected with the road system of Huhang and Zhabei districts and form a whole. This is the city's overall plan for reorganizing the old urban area. In the past three years, a total of 46 li of new roads have been added, 101 li of roads have been rebuilt, 37 li of ditches have been buried, 45 bridges of various sizes have been built, 16 wharves, and more than 1,000 meters of embankments. The projects that are about to be held include the construction of Wenmiao Park, the burial of Puzhao River ditches, the opening of Ximen Road, and the widening of Limalu. Since the widening of Dongmen Road, the advantages and disadvantages of the city's road construction levy regulations have been obvious to everyone, and the revitalization of the market and the increase in land prices are even more remarkable facts. I dare to believe that in the future, widening the old roads will not only be difficult for the citizens, but also many will be willing to organize it themselves. At the same time, related to the reorganization of the old urban area, is a citizen-built project. In the past three years, the city's annual construction has increased from more than 3.13 million yuan to 15 million yuan, which proves the progress of construction over the years. In other words, it is not the effect of reorganizing the old urban area. However, the holding of the project requires a lot of money. At this time, the city's funds have not reached a prosperous state, and the implementation of the entire plan is difficult to complete in one go. It can only be carried out step by step, and it is not easy to plan for long-term and rapid results.

Building the city center area, Shanghai's position, in terms of the country, has become the largest commercial port, and in terms of the world, it also occupies a considerable position. However, the so-called prosperous area is only a small area of the concession. In the future, if we want to further develop Shanghai, we must use a long-term vision and make careful and detailed plans, which is not enough to meet the needs of the future. When examining the shortcomings of the current Shanghai municipal administration, the most important ones are the following three: (1) The concession lies across the center of the city, so that the traffic between Huhang and Zhabei is separated and the facilities cannot be unified. (2) Shanghai's waterways and railways cannot be connected to each other, and the transportation of goods is not convenient and uneconomical. (3) In recent years, the tonnage of sea ships has increased sharply, and the existing wharf location and equipment are no longer applicable, so that most of the sea ships have to be anchored at the mouth of the Huangpu River. If a large-scale new port is not built quickly to accommodate giant ships, Shanghai's position as a commercial port in the world will inevitably be difficult to maintain. In terms of the current situation, the recovery of the concession is only a matter of time. After the recovery of the concession, the first shortcoming can be improved, but in order to remedy the second and third shortcomings, it is imperative to open the port of Wusong and add railways. If so, then the entire city center will inevitably move north from the concession to the Jiangwan area in the future. The terrain there is flat and the location is superior. It can connect the current commercial center and the new commercial port in the future, and is enough to be the hub of the entire city. And a piece of wilderness can be built on the ground without the trouble of improving the old urban area. Therefore, in the autumn of the 18th year, the municipal government delineated the area north of Xiangyin Road, south of Zhayin Road, east of Songhu Road, and west of Zhou Nan Shi Tu Yi Wu Tu as the city center area. In the past year, it has been actively planning and preparing for construction. The completed work includes the city's main road system and zoning plan, the city center area road system and the city center zoning plan, the municipal government building design, and the phased construction plan. All the layouts are based on the latest theories. Regarding the construction of railways, the selection of commercial port locations, the zoning of various industries, the smoothness of traffic, parks, forests, sports fields, and airport facilities, everything is well prepared. We also invited Chinese and foreign experts to carefully review it to show seriousness. Since the construction of trunk roads such as Songhu Road and Xiangzha Road began last winter, the progress has been exceptionally smooth. This autumn, the municipal government buildings will also be built in the city center administrative area to show promotion. However, the construction of the city center and commercial port involves many aspects, and the work is difficult and costly, which cannot be borne by the municipal government alone. The people of the whole city must work together with one heart to support the progress in order to succeed. To gain the support of the citizens, we must first seek the citizens' understanding of the significance of building a new urban area, then we can achieve twice the result with half the effort. For detailed information and planning instructions, refer to the "Planning Book for the Construction of the City Center Area", which will not be repeated here. As for public utilities, four new ferries have been added in Pujiang, two for long-distance voyages and two for short-distance voyages, and the fees are very low.

Xiong Shihui Received the Press Yesterday Morning 111

Three of the Four Injuries Have Healed

Reading Books and Newspapers as a Distraction in Bed

Xiong Shihui, the commander of the Songhu Garrison, received reporters from various newspapers at the Orthopedic Hospital on Xujiahui Road yesterday morning. Around 9:30, reporters from various newspapers arrived one after another. They were received by Wu Hongyu from the Orthopedic Hospital, and visited the entire hospital for a week. The various arrangements were in good order, especially the children's ward. At 10:15, Jiang Yi, the chief of the adjutant office of the Garrison Headquarters, and Li Dezhao, the chief of the military supply office, personally came out to receive them and led the reporters to ward No. 1 to meet Xiong. Xiong was wearing a gray spring cotton robe, lying on the bed, with a ruddy complexion and excellent spirits, but slightly thinner. Seeing the reporters arrive, he smiled and nodded, saying, "I haven't seen you for a long time." The reporters immediately expressed their condolences in detail. According to him, when the plane crashed, I was quite clear-headed. Even now, when I think back, the scene is vivid in my mind. The responsibility for the accident should be attributed to the pilot's poor skills. I heard that he was a retired pilot from the European War, and according to the rules, he should not be allowed to fly again. In short, with the immaturity of China's aviation industry today, we are subject to foreigners at every turn, which is regrettable. I have a total of four injuries, two head injuries have fully healed, the bandage on my left arm has been removed, and I can stretch freely. My right foot still needs to rest quietly, and the splint and bandage can be removed in more than a month. Lying on my back for many days, unable to turn over, is very painful. I heard that Yang Yongtai suffered internal injuries, and he can leave the hospital in three or four weeks. I have already eaten rice, and I read newspapers and various books in my spare time, so I am not so lonely. I am very grateful for the many visits and condolences from gentlemen from all walks of life. On Xiong's bedside, there were several books of Jiannan Poetry Collection and Suiyuan Poetry Talks. On the wall hung a couplet handwritten by Wang Yiting, with the line "There is nothing in sight, turning into brightness," which shows a sense of tranquility. It was already 10:40, and the reporters said goodbye and left. Zhang Qun, the mayor, went earlier than the reporters yesterday morning and talked for about ten minutes. The Huangpu River Bridge Problem 113

The Municipal Government Has Not Received a Concrete Plan

The talk of building a bridge over the Huangpu River has been rampant recently. The Public Concession Prohibits Dog Racing 114

The Mingyuan Board of Directors Expressed Its Dissatisfaction

The Attitude of the Public Works Bureau Has Not Changed

Regarding the problem of banning dog racing fields in the Public Concession, Fessenden, the director of the Public Works Bureau, based on the resolution of the Public Works Bureau Board of Directors, notified the two dog racing fields, Mingyuan and Shenyuan, at the beginning of the month, limiting them to close on March 31 of this year, etc. The details have been published in the previous newspaper. It is now known that McBain, the chairman of the Mingyuan Dog Racing Field, sent a letter to the Public Works Bureau on the 14th, expressing his dissatisfaction. The letter stated that dog racing is a legitimate business, and that the three-month deadline is not enough to end all affairs, and that the closure of the dog racing field will cause great losses to the rights of shareholders. He proposed that the provisions of the compensation amount be submitted to arbitration. A reporter from this newspaper visited Fessenden, the director of the Public Works Bureau, yesterday to inquire about the attitude of the Public Works Bureau after receiving the letter. Fessenden replied that he had not had the opportunity to submit the letter from Mingyuan to the Board of Directors. Roughly speaking, the Public Works Bureau Board of Directors can submit it for discussion at its regular meeting next Wednesday. He has no right to answer on behalf of the directors what their attitude is, but the resolution of the Public Works Bureau to order the dog racing field to close on March 31 will not change in any way. Therefore, the letter from the Mingyuan Dog Racing Field has absolutely no impact on the ban of the Public Works Bureau. The topic to be discussed at the next regular meeting of the Public Works Bureau Board of Directors will be the scope of the aftermath of the closure of the dog racing field at the end of March. As for the dog racing field's proposal to organize arbitration to resolve and remedy the losses, it is not impossible to do so.

Yihe Building Runner Shen Shou Kang Committed Suicide 116

Sacrificed Due to Economic Pressure

The Water Patrol Police Retrieved the Body

Shen Shou Kang, a building runner in the accounting room of Jardine Matheson & Co., committed suicide by jumping into the sea due to the inability to make up for the embezzlement of public funds. The following is a record of the information obtained by reporters from various parties through investigations:

The history of the deceased Shen Shou Kang, a building runner in the accounting room of Jardine Matheson & Co., was a native of Shaoxing, Zhejiang. He was only 25 years old. His father was an old servant in a foreign firm. There was no permanent property in the family. He had two brothers. Shou Kang was married and had a child each. Only his monthly salary was limited, and his family still lived in his hometown and did not come to Shanghai. He had a younger brother who was working in a money shop. He was usually serious in his work and had no habit of wandering and waste. He also lived in the firm.

Embezzlement of Public Funds Shen Shou Kang has been serving in the accounting room of Jardine Matheson & Co. for five or six years. His position is known as a building runner, which is to collect customer accounts, so he has funds in hand. It has been found that the salaries of the staff in the comprador section of Jardine Matheson & Co. are very meager. Senior staff members earn no more than forty or fifty yuan. Shen Shou Kang's monthly salary was only twenty-four yuan. How could he take care of his family with such a high level of living? Unable to make ends meet, the deficit was taken from the public funds collected. Over time, by the end of last month, the total amount used was more than two thousand yuan.

The Comprador Demanded Payment At the end of the year, according to commercial practice, the comprador of Jardine Matheson & Co. settled accounts with Shen, who handed over the remaining foreign currency. Shen had embezzled two thousand yuan. The comprador questioned where the money had gone. He said that his monthly salary was not enough to support his family, so he had gradually used it to support his family. The comprador, Mr. Pan, ordered him to pay the money in full, without any leniency. Shen, unable to raise the money at that time, conceived a pessimistic idea and jumped into the sea to commit suicide. It was a tragedy.

The Suicide Note Complained Shen was forced by the comprador to pay the money, and at that time, he said that he would wait to go out to raise the money. He left the firm last Saturday, never to return. Shen originally lived in the firm. His colleagues, seeing that he had suddenly not come, initially thought that he had returned to Shaoxing to raise money, and did not suspect anything else. It was not until the 14th of the previous day that the comprador of Jardine Matheson & Co., Mr. Pan, suddenly received a letter from Shen Shou Kang, in which the wording was very sad. He described that his family of several people relied entirely on his monthly salary of twenty-four yuan for food and clothing, and could not support them. He had no choice but to embezzle the account money. He used 2,000 yuan in a year, and there was no dissipation of wandering. Now, because he was forced to pay it back, there was no way to do it. He also said that with such a life, there was no hope of economic prosperity. Rather than living and suffering mentally, it was better to die. He decided to jump into the sea and die. By the time this letter arrived, he had already ended his life. There was another letter to his younger brother, with roughly the same wording. Both letters are now with Mr. Pan and his younger brother.

Reported to the Police and Searched for the Body The firm was very anxious about Shen's disappearance. Later, after receiving his letter, they knew that he had committed suicide. They urgently reported to his younger brother, and the younger brother also received his brother's suicide note. In grief, he went to the water patrol police station to report and searched for his body in the Huangpu River. It has not been found yet. Fearing that he had jumped into the sea in Wusong, they asked the water patrol police station to help them search for him.

A Fierce Battle Between Police and Bandits in Shark Port 117

Rescued the Hostages... Killed the Bandit Leader

Several bandit ships sneaked into Shark Port outside Wusongkou at about 4:00 a.m. the day before yesterday. The leaders were Zheng Changji and Xu San, two well-known Jiangnan kidnappers. They immediately led their men to land with weapons and hid in a small building on the edge of the port. The 18th team of the 4th district of the water police discovered this and reported to the brigade commander Lin Junsheng. After receiving the report, Brigade Commander Lin immediately led his team to rush to suppress the bandits together with the Haimen County police team. When they reached their destination, they saw that the bandits were all hiding in the building. They immediately ordered to open fire and shot at the small building. The bandits returned fire. They resisted stubbornly at first, but after fighting for more than an hour, they all rushed out of the door and fled back to the bandit ships. Bandit leader Xu San was shot and killed, and Zheng Changji was captured. They then used quick guns to sink a bandit ship. In this battle, they seized four rifles from the bandits and rescued Cui Jin, a hostage from Taicang, and Wang Jiaowa, a young girl from Changshu. They have been sent back to their hometowns separately.

All Five Hostages Rescued

The Zhongshan warship rescued the hostages. After the Zhaoshang Bureau's New Ming steamer was robbed in the Min Sea, General Manager Li Zhonggong immediately telegraphed the authorities in Fujian, Xiamen, and Guangdong, requesting them to send warships to pursue the fleeing bandits and rescue the kidnapped individuals. They also requested your honor to forward the request to the Naval Headquarters, sending telegrams to assist in the investigation to comfort the families of the robbed. Submitted jointly by the Min and Xiamen bureau chiefs.

Surveyor Inspects Lost Goods. The surveyor will directly inspect and report the lost and damaged goods inside the ship to inform the guests. Then, based on the surveyor's report of lost and damaged goods, procedures for handling compensation will be carried out.

Re-Telegraphing the Navy to Pursue Bandits. Yesterday, General Manager Li also telegraphed the Naval Headquarters, urging them to quickly order Xiamen warships to pursue and suppress the fleeing bandits in separate directions and to recover the stolen goods. He also discussed with the Chief of the Shipping Section and the Chief of the Business Section the installation of iron nets on naval vessels and the deployment of armed guards to ensure safety.

Car and Train Collide Violently 120

Car Thrown into River

Passengers and Driver Unharmed

Yesterday morning at 11:45, a Western engineer from the Kailuan Company, Bi Shidong, hired a No. 17664 (City No. 563) commercial car from the Zha Pu Road Dada Automobile Company to go to the Rihui Bridge outside the South City to work. The car was driven by driver Li Shouchu. When the car reached the vicinity of the railway on Da Yong Road, heading south to north, the driver accelerated, intending to cross the railway.
